     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Ottawa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ottawageegees.png" class="image"><img alt="Stylized horse logo of the University of Ottawa athletics program, the Gee-Gees" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/66/Ottawageegees.png" width="125" height="125" class="thumbimage" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ottawageegees.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Varsity team logo is a horse because &quot;gee gee&quot; may also refer to the lead horse in a race
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Gee-Gees" title="Ottawa Gee-Gees">Ottawa Gee-Gees</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Athletics and student recreation at the University are managed by Sports Services.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Varsity teams compete in either <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> or <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9seau_du_sport_%C3%A9tudiant_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="R&eacute;seau du sport &eacute;tudiant du Qu&eacute;bec" class="mw-redirect">R&eacute;seau du sport &eacute;tudiant du Qu&eacute;bec</a> conference of Canadian Interuniversity Sport, varying by team. The University hosts 29 competitive clubs, including 11 varsity.<sup id="cite_ref-sport_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sport-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The first athletic group at the University was formed in 1885, with garnet and grey becoming the official team colours. Shortly thereafter, garnet and grey became the official colours of the University.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Varsity team's names are a play on the initials of the colours. Varsity teams did not immediately adopt a name, leading others to refer to them by their colours. Ottawa sports media referred to the teams as &quot;GG&quot; for the teams and eventually the shorthand became official.<sup id="cite_ref-sport_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sport-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Because the term gee gee also describes the lead horse in a race, that animal became their mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-sport_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sport-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University owns and operates three athletic facilities on the University's two campuses. Montpetit Hall and Minto Sports Complex are located on the main campus and another is located on Lees.<sup id="cite_ref-spofac_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spofac-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> The Minto Sports Complex houses the University's arena ice rinks, which seat 840. All facilities are shared with both recreational users, as well as varsity teams.<sup id="cite_ref-spofac_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spofac-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> The University planned a new 3,500 seat stadium for its varsity football team for the <a href="/wiki/2012_CIS_football_season" title="2012 CIS football season">2012 CIS football season</a>. The new stadium is due to the extensive renovations taking place at their former arena, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Clair_Stadium" title="Frank Clair Stadium">Frank Clair Stadium</a> and the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Lansdowne_Park" title="Lansdowne Park">Lansdowne Park</a>, both of which belong to the City of Ottawa.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As is mandatory for Canadian Interuniversity Sport, the University does not provide full-ride athletic scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> On the recreational level, the University's Sports Services operates intramural sport leagues and tournaments with a participation rate of 1 of 8 students. Sports include badminton, volleyball, basketball, swimming, soccer and martial arts.<sup id="cite_ref-sport_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sport-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people_and_alumni">Notable people and alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Ottawa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notable people and alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Ottawa_people" title="List of University of Ottawa people">List of University of Ottawa people</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Paul_martin_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The Prime Minister of Canada, Paul Martin, former alumni of University of Ottawa" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Paul_martin_2004.jpg/170px-Paul_martin_2004.jpg" width="170" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Paul_martin_2004.jpg/255px-Paul_martin_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Paul_martin_2004.jpg/340px-Paul_martin_2004.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Paul_martin_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Paul Martin, the 24th Prime Minister of Canada was educated at the University of Ottawa
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Graduates have found success in many fields, serving as the heads of diverse institutions in both public and private sectors. As of 18 October 2011, the University has 167,224 alumni.<sup id="cite_ref-Quick_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quick-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Faculty and graduates have accumulated numerous awards including <a href="/wiki/Governor_General%27s_Awards" title="Governor General's Awards">Governor General's Awards</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Fiction" title="Pulitzer Prize for Fiction">Pulitzer Prize for Fiction</a>. Recipients of the Governor General's Award include <a href="/wiki/Michel_Bock" title="Michel Bock">Michel Bock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christl_Verduyn" title="Christl Verduyn">Christl Verduyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Carol_Shields" title="Carol Shields">Carol Shields</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Chancellors have previously held positions such as <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viceregal_consort_of_Canada" title="Viceregal consort of Canada">Viceregal consort of Canada</a>. Examples include, <a href="/wiki/Pauline_Vanier" title="Pauline Vanier">Pauline Vanier</a>, 46th Viceregal consort of Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_L%C3%A9ger" title="Gabrielle L&eacute;ger">Gabrielle L&eacute;ger</a>, the 48th Viceregal consort of Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Sauv%C3%A9" title="Maurice Sauv&eacute;">Maurice Sauv&eacute;</a>, the 50th Viceregal consort of Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Micha%C3%ABlle_Jean" title="Micha&euml;lle Jean">Micha&euml;lle Jean</a>, the 27th Governor General of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Two former <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">heads of government</a> attended the University, including <a href="/wiki/Edward_Morris,_1st_Baron_Morris" title="Edward Morris, 1st Baron Morris">Edward Morris, 1st Baron Morris</a>, the 2nd <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Newfoundland" title="Prime Minister of Newfoundland" class="mw-redirect">Prime Minister of Newfoundland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Martin" title="Paul Martin">Paul Martin</a>, the 24th <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Premiers include <a href="/wiki/Paul_Okalik" title="Paul Okalik">Paul Okalik</a>, 1st <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Nunavut" title="Premier of Nunavut">Premier of Nunavut</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dalton_McGuinty" title="Dalton McGuinty">Dalton McGuinty</a>, 24th <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Ontario" title="Premier of Ontario">Premier of Ontario</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Five graduates became <a href="/wiki/Puisne_Justice" title="Puisne Justice" class="mw-redirect">puisine justices</a>, with one moving on to become a <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Canada" title="Chief Justice of Canada">Chief Justice of Canada</a>. Puisne Justices include <a href="/wiki/Louise_Arbour" title="Louise Arbour">Louise Arbour</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michel_Bastarache" title="Michel Bastarache">Michel Bastarache</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Louise_Charron" title="Louise Charron">Louise Charron</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Louis_LeBel" title="Louis LeBel">Louis LeBel</a><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rald_Fauteux" title="G&eacute;rald Fauteux">G&eacute;rald Fauteux</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Fauteux would later become a Chief Justice of Canada.</p> 
     <p>Prominent business leaders include <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Lamarre" title="Daniel Lamarre">Daniel Lamarre</a>, president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Cirque_du_Soleil" title="Cirque du Soleil">Cirque du Soleil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Desmarais" title="Paul Desmarais">Paul Desmarais</a>, chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Power_Corporation_of_Canada" title="Power Corporation of Canada">Power Corporation of Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Desmarais" title="Andr&eacute; Desmarais">Andr&eacute; Desmarais</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> Calin Rovinescu, President and CEO of Air Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Ouellet" title="Andr&eacute; Ouellet">Andr&eacute; Ouellet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Postmaster_General_of_Canada" title="Postmaster General of Canada">Postmaster General of Canada</a>, CEO and president of <a href="/wiki/Canada_Post" title="Canada Post">Canada Post</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

       <li><span id="CITEREFPr.C3.A9vost2008" class="citation">Pr&eacute;vost, Michel (2008), <i>L?Universit&eacute; d?Ottawa depuis 1848 / The University of Ottawa since 1848</i>, Ottawa, Ontario: Universit&eacute; d?Ottawa / University of Ottawa</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUniversity+of+Ottawa&amp;rft.aufirst=Michel&amp;rft.aulast=Pr%C3%A9vost&amp;rft.au=Pr%C3%A9vost%2C+Michel&amp;rft.btitle=L%E2%80%99Universit%C3%A9+d%E2%80%99Ottawa+depuis+1848+%2F+The+University+of+Ottawa+since+1848&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.place=Ottawa%2C+Ontario&amp;rft.pub=Universit%C3%A9+d%E2%80%99Ottawa+%2F+University+of+Ottawa&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></li>
